PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] No. 711 Philadelphia, 1980, Appeal from Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Philadelphia County, Nos. 1505 May Term, 1977, 1155-1157 June Term, 1977 and 861, 907 July Term, 1977.

 

528 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Stayton


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


314 Pa. Super. 12; 460 A.2d 349; 1983 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3100


October 20, 1981, Argued  
May 13, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 29 Philadelphia, 1981, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Susquehanna County at No. 283, 1980.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Susquehanna County (Pennsylvania), which upheld a fine imposed upon him pursuant to 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 4943, for operating an overweight vehicle. Defendant's suppression motion, requesting that the evidence of the truck's weight be suppressed as illegally obtained, was denied.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was fined for driving an overweight truck on an interstate, under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 4943. Defendant unsuccessfully moved to suppress evidence of his truck's weight, which he asserted was illegally obtained because the Commonwealth had no right to conduct a "spot check" of his vehicle to determine whether it was overweight. The court affirmed. The court held that the arresting officer had probable cause to direct that the weight of the truck be checked. The officer's observations provided him with sufficient cause to order the weight checked as the travelling of a truck such as defendant's at a slow rate of speed up an incline was certainly an indication that the vehicle may have been overweight. Defendant argued that the officer's observations as to defendant's speed were contradicted by defendant in certain aspects. Such factual determinations, however, were for the trial court. Thus, the court held that the officer's training and experience, when coupled with his observation of defendant's speed in relation to other commercial vehicles, provided him with sufficient cause to check the truck for its weight.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order imposing defendant's fine. The court held that the arresting officer had probable and sufficient cause to direct that the weight of defendant's truck be checked because he observed the truck travelling at a slow rate of speed up an incline.

 

529 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Potts


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


314 Pa. Super. 256; 460 A.2d 1127; 1983 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2970


January 11, 1983, Argued  
April 29, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 1228 Pittsburgh 1980, No. 1229 Pittsburgh 1980, Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Allegheny County at No. 7903596 and 7903595.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which was entered upon a verdict finding her guilty of prostitution, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5902(a)(1), and conspiracy, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 903(a)(1). Defendant argued that § 5902(a)(1) was overbroad and vague, that the evidence was insufficient, that prejudicial evidence was admitted, and that the trial court erred in its jury charge.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of prostitution under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5902(a)(1), and conspiracy under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 903(a)(1). She appealed and argued that § 5902(a)(1) was overbroad and vague, the evidence was insufficient, prejudicial evidence was admitted, and the trial court erred in its jury charge. The court affirmed and ruled that the statute needed only to convey sufficiently definite warning of the conduct proscribed when measured by common understanding and practices, that prostitution had acquired a traditional meaning of indiscriminate illicit intercourse for hire, and that § 5902(a)(1) was not overbroad or vague. The court ruled that the officer's testimony that he knew defendant previously did not link her to prior crimes and was not prejudicial, and that the trial court correctly refused to charge on issues not raised by the evidence. The court also found that evidence that defendant offered for a price to engage in sexual acts described in words commonly used by prostitutes, accepted the money, and undressed in preparation, was sufficient to prove that she was then engaging in sexual activity as a business, and that actual intercourse was not required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for prostitution and conspiracy. The court ruled that the statute was not overbroad or vague and afforded sufficient warning of the conduct proscribed, that police testimony of prior knowledge of the defendant did not link her to prior criminal conduct, that the trial court properly refused points for charge not raised by the evidence, and that the guilty verdict was supported by sufficient evidence.

Commonwealth v. Chance


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


312 Pa. Super. 435; 458 A.2d 1371; 1983 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2864


June 3, 1981, Submitted  
April 8, 1983, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied October 3, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 1447 Philadelphia, 1980, Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Delaware County at No. 6405 of 1978.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of his convictions for criminal attempt to commit rape; possession of an instrument of crime; possession of firearms without a license; crimes committed with firearms; and two counts each of aggravated assault; simple assault; terroristic threats; and recklessly endangering another person from the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania).


OVERVIEW: Appellant prisoner contended that there was insufficient evidence to sustain his conviction of attempted rape, aggravated assault, and terroristic threats. Upon a review of the evidence the court held that there was sufficient evidence to support appellant's convictions. The court held that appellant's contention that the information was improper because it was not manually signed but stamped with a facsimile of a signature was waived, because appellant failed to preserve the allegation of error through the proper pretrial motion. Appellant argued that it was error to have convicted him of having committed crimes with firearms pursuant to 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6103. The court held that appellant's conviction under § 6103 was in error because § 6103, was not intended to create a separately punishable crime under the Uniform Firearms Act. The court vacated the suspended sentence imposed for the conviction. The court did not remand for resentencing despite the vacated potion of the sentence because the court's action had no effect on the sentences imposed upon those offenses of which appellant was lawfully convicted.


OUTCOME: Appellant prisoner's convictions and sentences were affirmed, except appellant's conviction of having committed a crime with a firearm because the relevant statute did not intend to create a separately punishable crime.

Commonwealth v. Quartman


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


312 Pa. Super. 349; 458 A.2d 994; 1983 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2836


January 18, 1983, Submitted  
March 31, 1983, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied July 20, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 2991 Philadelphia 1981, Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Lycoming County, Criminal Division, at No. 81-10,066.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lycoming County (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of rape, deviant sexual intercourse, simple assault, and terroristic threats and sentenced him to three-to-six years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with rape, deviate sexual intercourse, simple assault, and terroristic threats following appellant's encounter with a fellow inmate. The trial court found that evidence of the victim's prior sexual relations with other inmates was inadmissible to impeach the victim's credibility and to imply consent between appellant and the victim. A jury found appellant guilty of all charges, and appellant was sentenced to three-to-six years imprisonment. Appellant alleged that the exclusion of evidence of the victim's prior sexual relations denied his Sixth Amendment right to confrontation. The court affirmed, holding that because appellant offered no special circumstances to outweigh the state's interest in shielding the victim from marginally relevant evidence concerning the victim's prior sexual relations, the Pennsylvania Rape Shield Law, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3104 was constitutional in its application to appellant's case. The court further held that appellant's contention that the jury charge should have informed the jury that the Pennsylvania Rape Shield Law prevented appellant from introducing evidence of the victim's sexual history was without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order convicting and sentencing appellant on charges of rape, deviant sexual intercourse, simple assault, and terroristic threats because the trial court's exclusion of evidence concerning the victim's prior sexual history was proper under the Pennsylvania Rape Shield Law, and there was no error in refusing to inform the jury that such evidence was excluded by statute.

Commonwealth v. Maxwell


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


312 Pa. Super. 557; 459 A.2d 362; 1983 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2802


May 11, 1982, Argued  
March 25, 1983, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument Denied May 25, 1983. Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied November 18, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 1760 Philadelphia, 1981, Appeal from Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas Trial Division, Criminal Section, of Philadelphia County at No. C.P. 80-02-2235 and 2237, No. 1764 Philadelphia, 1981, Appeal from Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Trial Division, Criminal Section of Philadelphia County at No. 2235-2264 February Term, 1980.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant and the prosecution both sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which convicted defendant of two counts of robbery and sentenced him to concurrent terms of probation and a fine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and charged with two counts of robbery. Prior to the trial, defendant filed a motion pursuant to Pa. R. Crim. P. 1101 to waive a trial by jury. The prosecution opposed the request and asserted an absolute right to a jury trial pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5104(c). The trial court denied defendant's motion. He was convicted on both counts of robbery, sentenced to concurrent terms of probation, and fined. The prosecution then filed a motion to modify sentence, requesting that the trial court sentence defendant as a repeat offender. Both the prosecution and defendant appealed. The court reversed and remanded the trial court's judgment, with instructions that if defendant were to resubmit a motion for waiver of a jury trial, the trial court should proceed in accordance with Rule 1101. The court held that, while judicial economy was a concern, the trial court did not have the benefit of a recent holding that § 5104(c) was unconstitutional. The court concluded that the trial court erred in failing to examine and weigh defendant's reasons for wanting a non-jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's judgment with instructions that if defendant were to resubmit a motion for waiver of a jury trial, the trial court should place on the record a colloquy between it and defendant.

Commonwealth v. Speller


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


311 Pa. Super. 569; 458 A.2d 198; 1983 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2714


October 19, 1982, Submitted  
March 11, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 299 Philadelphia, 1981, Appeal from Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Philadelphia County, No. 1658 March Term, 1980.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which convicted defendant of making terroristic threats, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2706, a misdemeanor, and harassment, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2709, a summary offense. Defendant claimed that the evidence was insufficient, that he was improperly tried for harassment, that evidentiary rulings were prejudicial, and that trial counsel was ineffective.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for making terroristic threats, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2706, and harassment, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2709, claiming that the evidence was insufficient, that he was improperly tried for harassment, that evidentiary rulings were prejudicial, and that trial counsel was ineffective. The court held that there was sufficient evidence to convict on section 2706, and that evidence about prior convictions and other incidents was admissible because it was probative of defendant's intent in the present case. However, defendant was improperly convicted of section 2709 because it was not alleged in the information that charged defendant with section 2706. Consequently, defendant, in complete violation of U.S. Const. amend. VI and Pa. Const. art. I, § 9, was convicted of a crime for which he was never formally charged and that was not part of the charged offense. Because defendant's charge of ineffective counsel could not be resolved from the record but may have had merit, the court vacated the conviction as to the harassment, but vacated and remanded on the terroristic threats charge, to determine if there was ineffective counsel.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's conviction for harassment because, unconstitutionally, he was never formally charged with harassment in the indictment that brought him before the trial court. The conviction was vacated as to making terrorist threats but remanded to determine defendant's claim of ineffective counsel.

Spidle v. Livingston Constr. Co.


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


311 Pa. Super. 201; 457 A.2d 565; 1983 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2774


March 22, 1982, Argued  
March 11, 1983, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied October 11, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 38 Harrisburg, 1981, Appeal from the Order of January 29, 1981 in the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Civil Action at No. 1413 S 1979.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corporation appealed an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania), sustaining defendant employer's demurrer to the corporation's attempt to join the employer in plaintiff employee's negligence suit. Defendant claimed that the employer could be joined in order to determine the proportion of causal negligence attributable to it under the Comparative Negligence Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 7102.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff employee was injured in the course of his employment through the negligence of a third party, defendant corporation. Plaintiff sued defendant corporation. Defendant joined defendant employer. Defendant demurred, claiming that it was immune from suit. The trial court sustained the objections. On appeal, the corporation claimed that the employer could be joined as an additional defendant in order to determine the proportion of causal negligence attributable to it under the Comparative Negligence Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 7102. Defendant also claimed that an amendment to the Workers' Compensation Act, 77 P.S. 481 was unconstitutional. The appellate court affirmed and held that workers' compensation was the only remedy available to employees against their employers, joinder was improper. Joinder would place the economic burden on the employer to participate in the trial and could lead to an inflated verdict and defeat the purpose of the worker's compensation act. The court found that the amendment was constitutional because the amendment's title gave sufficient notice to third parties that the liability of an employer for damages, contribution, or indemnity had changed.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's sustaining of defendant employer's demurrer to defendant corporation's motion to join the employer in plaintiff employer's negligence suit. The court held that because the workers' compensation law was an employee's sole remedy against an employer, and joinder would thwart the purposes of the worker's compensation law, joinder was properly denied.

 

536 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


CHIESA v. FETCHKO


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


1983 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2567



February 18, 1983 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Opinion Withdrawn March 25, 1983


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 117 Pittsburgh, 1982, Appeal from the Order entered January 19, 1982, Court of Common Pleas, Allegheny County, Civil Action, Law at No. GD 81-00477.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Pennsylvania Department of Public Welfare sought review of the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas, Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which denied appellant's petition to intervene in appellee beneficiary's medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: Appellee beneficiary filed a medical malpractice action against defendant doctors under the Health Care Services Malpractice Act, 40 P.S. § 1301.101 et seq. Appellee received both Medicaid and cash assistance from appellant Pennsylvania Department of Public Welfare, but did not notify it of the pendency of the action. Appellee's medical malpractice claim was settled, and appellant presented a petition to intervene to the trial court. The trial court ordered the settlement monies placed in escrow, and then denied appellant's petition. Appellant sought review, and the court reversed the judgment denying the petition and remanded the case for further proceedings. The court found that 62 P.S. § 1409(b)(1) clearly gave appellant the right to recover the reasonable value of benefits provided to appellee from the defendant doctors. The action never reached trial on the facts, so 62 P.S. § 1409(b)(5) permitted appellant to become a party to or to consolidate its action with that of appellee. The court found that appellee had the duty to notify appellant of her medical malpractice action, and because appellant did not receive notice, its petition should have been granted.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which denied appellant Pennsylvania Department of Public Welfare's petition to intervene in appellee beneficiary's medical malpractice action. Under Pennsylvania law, appellant had the right to recover the reasonable value of benefits provided to appellee from the defendant doctors. Appellant did not receive notice of the action, and, therefore, its petition should not have been denied.

Commonwealth v. Laing


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


310 Pa. Super. 105; 456 A.2d 204; 1983 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2497


October 13, 1982, Argued  
February 4, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 1199 Pittsburgh, 1981, Appeal from Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Venango County, No. 336-1980


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas, of Venango County (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of four counts of aggravated assault, four counts of recklessly endangering another person, simple assault, and leaving the scene of an accident.


OVERVIEW: During a drunken brawl, defendant drove his van down the sidewalk, striking two people and narrowly missing two others. The trial court convicted defendant of four counts of aggravated assault, four counts of recklessly endangering another person, one count of simple assault, and leaving the scene of an accident. Sentences were set to run concurrently in three of the aggravated assaults, the reckless endangerment charges, and leaving the scene of an accident. An additional consecutive sentence was added for the fourth aggravated assault case. On appeal, the court held that 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 308, which provided that voluntary intoxication was not a defense to criminal charges, did not offend the constitutional guarantees of equal protection and due process. The court held that it was proper to charge and convict appellant on several offenses for a single criminal act but that only one sentence could be imposed. The judgment of sentence was vacated and the case remanded for resentencing on the convictions of aggravated assault and leaving the scene of an accident.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of sentence for defendant's conviction of four counts of aggravated assault, four counts of recklessly endangering another person, one count of simple assault, and leaving the scene of an accident. The court remanded for resentencing on the convictions of aggravated assault and leaving the scene of an accident because only one sentence could be imposed for a single criminal act.

 

539 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Rumsey


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


309 Pa. Super. 137; 454 A.2d 1121; 1983 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2346


September 9, 1980, Argued  
January 7, 1983, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 2564 October, 1979, Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Criminal Division, at No. 4814-78.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of a judgment of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), imposed on convictions for aggravated assault, assault by a prisoner, recklessly endangering another person, and simple assault. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in disallowing evidence of intoxication under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 308 (Supp. 1974 to 1981).


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate was arrested for allegedly assaulting prison guards by swinging a sharpened scissors at them. The trial court refused to allow evidence that appellant had been drunk on bootleg wine and unable to form the requisite mental intent. Appellant was found guilty of aggravated assault, assault by a prisoner, recklessly endangering another person, and simple assault. He appealed contending that 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 308 (Supp. 1974 to 1981), which limited the use of voluntary intoxication evidence at criminal trials, was unconstitutional. The court affirmed, finding that the legislature acted within permissible constitutional bounds in enacting § 308. Voluntary intoxication was within the control of the actor, and unlike insanity of diminished capacity, did not result from a disease or defect of the mind. The curtailment of the defensive relevance of voluntary intoxication did not run afoul of the equal protection or cruel and unusual punishment clauses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of sentence, imposed on appellant inmate's convictions for aggravated assault, assault by a prisoner, recklessly endangering another person, and simple assault. The court held that the legislature acted within permissible constitutional bounds in deciding to limit the defensive use of voluntary intoxication evidence in criminal trials.

Commonwealth v. Stauffer


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


309 Pa. Super. 176; 454 A.2d 1140; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 6073


January 6, 1982, Argued  
December 30, 1982, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied April 19, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 1541 Philadelphia, 1981, Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence in the Court of Common Pleas of Lycoming County, Criminal Division at No. 79-10 680.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former state department director challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lycoming County (Pennsylvania) that sentenced him after he was convicted by a jury of unlawfully soliciting political contributions from classified civil service employees.


OVERVIEW: Appellant former state department director was charged with and convicted of unlawfully soliciting political contributions from classified civil service employees. He complained that the trial court erred in allowing an amendment to the information, that the statute was vague and overbroad, that his prosecution was selective and discriminatory, that testimony was improperly admitted, that the judge's charge was inadequate, and that his sentence was an abuse of discretion. The court affirmed the conviction because it found that the amendment to the information corrected an error but did not charge an additional or different offense. 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 5552(c)(2) appropriately restricted political activities and was clear and specific, and there was no evidence on the record to support an allegation of discriminatory enforcement. The court allowed the other crime evidence that was barred by the statute of limitations because it was not overly prejudicial and it tended to be connected to the charges tried and to show that appellant was the person who committed the charged crimes. Appellant failed to preserve errors in sentencing for appellate review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed because the amendment to the information did not charge an additional or different offense. The statute restricted political activities, was clear and specific, and there was no evidence to support an allegation of discriminatory enforcement. The court allowed the other crime evidence because it was not overly prejudicial and it was connected and showed that appellant was the person who committed the charged crimes.

Krenzelak v. Krenzelak


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


307 Pa. Super. 499; 453 A.2d 998; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 5871


April 28, 1982, Argued  
December 10, 1982, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted February 10, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 1042 Pittsburgh, 1981, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, Washington County, at No. 7810, in Equity, Book 45, Pg. 123.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-wife sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas, Washington County (Pennsylvania), which sustained preliminary objections by appellees, ex-husband and his son, to appellant's complaint in equity to set aside the conveyance of a property from appellee ex-husband to appellee son.


OVERVIEW: Appellee ex-husband filed a divorce action against appellant ex-wife in April 1978, and appellant filed against appellee ex-husband in April 1979. In March 1980, appellee ex-husband transferred property to appellee ex-husband's son for no monetary value. The lower court sustained appellees' preliminary objections to set aside the conveyance. On appeal, the court reversed the order. The court ruled that the Divorce Code of Pennsylvania (Code), 23 P.S. § 101 et seq. applied, as appellant made application to proceed under the Code, and appellees made no opposition. 23 P.S. § 403(d) authorized a nullification of any disposition of property by appellee ex-husband to appellee ex-husband's son, because the son had notice of the pending divorce and paid a wholly inadequate consideration for the property. The court found that the parties' situation must have been considered as it existed up to the date of the first divorce filing, when appellee ex-husband still owned the property. The court further found that such a retroactive application was constitutional as a proper exercise of the legislature's police power in providing for the distribution of property upon divorce.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that sustained preliminary objections by appellees, ex-husband and son, because the property conveyed between appellees was for no monetary consideration, occurred almost two years after appellee ex-husband filed for divorce and eleven months after appellant filed her divorce action, and property acquired during the marriage was classified as marital property for equitable distribution purposes.

 

543 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Lewis


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


307 Pa. Super. 468; 453 A.2d 982; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 5854


April 12, 1982, Argued  
November 30, 1982, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 1057 APRIL TERM, 1979, Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Allegheny County, No. 7802983-A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) that convicted her of misdemeanor barratry, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5109, for intentionally filing numerous unjust and vexatious lawsuits against her former husband.


OVERVIEW: Following her antagonistic divorce from her husband, defendant brought eight lawsuits against him, accusing him of, inter alia, assault, property damage, conspiracy, and emotional distress. The suits were all dismissed. Defendant was then charged with misdemeanor barratry, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5109, which prohibited vexing others with unjust and vexatious suits. The jury found her guilty and she was sentenced to six to 12 months in jail. Defendant appealed. In affirming, the court ruled that § 5109, which restated the common law standard for barratry, was not void for vagueness under the Due Process Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The statute was sufficiently specific in light of defendant's particular conduct and it contained a standard sufficiently normative to inform defendant that her conduct was in violation thereof. Moreover, the evidence, viewed in the light most favorable to the commonwealth, was sufficient for the jury to find beyond a reasonable doubt that her suits were unjust and in most cases entirely groundless.


OUTCOME: The barratry conviction was affirmed because it was supported by sufficient evidence, viewed in the light most favorable to the commonwealth, that the suits which defendant caused to be filed were unjust, and because the barratry statute, which embodied common law norms, was not unconstitutionally vague, but gave defendant adequate notice that her conduct was in violation thereof.

Commonwealth v. Gotto


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


306 Pa. Super. 434; 452 A.2d 803; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 5744


March 10, 1980, Argued  
November 19, 1982, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied May 9, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 1141 October Term, 1979, Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Northampton County, Criminal Division, at No. 2174 of 1977


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Northampton County (Pennsylvania), which convicted defendant of homicide by vehicle, driving while under the influence of alcohol, and meeting of vehicles proceeding in the opposite direction.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to being convicted of homicide by vehicle and driving while under the influence of alcohol, defendant argued that the homicide by vehicle statute was unconstitutional and contrary to common law and that the trial court erred in admitting evidence of a blood-alcohol test. Relying on its prior case law, the court first held that the homicide by vehicle statute, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3732, was constitutionally valid and did not violate common law. The court then held that the error, if any, was harmless in failing to advise defendant of her right to a breath test prior to testing a blood sample to determine whether defendant was intoxicated. In so holding, the court noted that the test in the case at issue was performed on a sample of blood previously taken from defendant and did not require an additional invasion of defendant's body. The court then held that defendant effectively waived her Miranda rights prior to giving a statement to police because defendant was aware of the criminal transaction the police were investigating. Thus, the court affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for homicide by vehicle, driving while under the influence of alcohol, and meeting of vehicles proceeding in the opposite direction because the trial court did not err in ruling on the admission of evidence and properly charged the jury.

Petri v. Smith


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


307 Pa. Super. 261; 453 A.2d 342; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 5484


February 3, 1982, Argued  
October 22, 1982, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument Denied December 30, 1982. Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied May 16, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 1968 Philadelphia, 1981, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, of Philadelphia County, June Term, 1979, No. 2798.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, individually and as guardian of her minor son, sought review of the grant of summary judgment, in favor of appellee doctor and pharmaceutical company, from the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) in appellant's medical malpractice action.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, individually and as guardian of her minor son, contended that the trial court erred when it granted summary judgment in favor of appellee doctor and pharmaceutical company in her malpractice action. Appellant brought suit for alleged negligence in the delivery of her son, 14 years after he was born. Appellees contended that summary judgment was appropriate because the statute of limitations had run. The court stated that in the application of the discovery rule, three independent phases of knowledge must have been known or knowable to appellant before the limitation period commenced. The court stated that appellant knew of the injuries to her son and the operative cause of the injuries shortly after his birth. The court stated that the record did not demonstrate whether appellant had knowledge of the causative relationship between the injury and the operative conduct phase until she filed suit 14 years after her son's birth. The court held that the question of whether appellant was reasonable when she failed to discover the injury prior to the running of the period of limitation was a jury question. The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment.


OUTCOME: Trial court's grant of summary judgment was vacated and remanded because whether appellant, individually and as guardian of her minor son, failed to discover the injury prior to the running of the statute of limitations was a question for the jury.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas, Erie County (Pennsylvania), which terminated her parental rights to her infant son pursuant to 1 P.S. § 311 (1970).


OVERVIEW: Appellant mother challenged the judgment of the lower court's termination of her parental rights to her son. Appellant argued that appellee, Children's Services of Erie County, failed to meet its burden of proof. Appellant was 14 years old and in the seventh grade, when she gave birth to her son. During the first year of his life, appellant cared for the child while living at home with her parents. The state, acting parens patriae, found appellant to be a delinquent. An incident took place wherein the appellant's parents found the child outside and unconscious. The child was placed in foster care and a caseworker began to see appellant. Appellant testified as to her efforts to comply with goals she had set with the caseworker. The evidence showed that appellant regularly visited the child. The court reversed, finding that the evidence failed to support a finding that appellant evidenced a settled purpose of relinquishing her parental rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment that terminated appellant mother's parental rights was reversed. The court found that the evidence failed to support a finding that appellant evidenced a settled purpose of relinquishing her parental rights because while the child was in foster care, appellant visited him regularly and frequently up until the time that her visitation privileges were cut off.

Commonwealth v. Pringle


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


304 Pa. Super. 67; 450 A.2d 103; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 5152


February 16, 1982, Argued  
September 3, 1982, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied January 18, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 1968 Philadelphia, 1980, Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County, at No. 190 Criminal 1980


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County (Pennsylvania), which convicted her of disorderly conduct.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was involved in an incident wherein she protested a friend's arrest by repeatedly shouting crude epithets at the arresting officers in front of a large crowd. She was subsequently convicted of disorderly conduct. Appellant challenged her conviction, contending that the provisions of the disorderly conduct statute were unconstitutionally vague and overbroad in violation of U.S. Const. amend. I and U.S. Const. amend. IV, and that the words she used were not obscene or fighting words. Affirming appellant's conviction, the court held that the statute was constitutional, and that in calling the officers "goddamn fucking pigs", appellant used obscene language within the contemplated context of the disorderly conduct statute. The court further held that, even if the words were not considered obscene, they constituted fighting words and created a risk of public alarm and the incitement of lawless behavior. The court did, however, vacate appellant's sentence and remanded to permit the lower court to specify its reasons for dispensing with a pre-sentence report.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for disorderly conduct because the words in question constituted obscene language and, in the alternative, were fighting words which created the risk of inciting the crowd into unlawful behavior. However, the court vacated the sentence and remanded for the lower court to specify its reasons for dispensing with the pre-sentence report.

 

548 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Hollis


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


304 Pa. Super. 1; 450 A.2d 70; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 5079


March 18, 1980, Argued  
August 27, 1982, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied December 22, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: Nos. 297 & 1006 October Term, 1979, Appeals from the Order and Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Criminal Division, No. 4489-78.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which denied appellant's pretrial motion to quash the information for successive prosecutions under Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 110 and which convicted appellant of driving under the influence although the denial of the motion to quash was on appeal.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with the misdemeanor of driving while under the influence of alcohol and the summary offense of fleeing or attempting to elude a police officer. The summary charge was withdrawn. Appellant waived his right to a preliminary hearing on the drunken driving charge. Appellant sought to quash the information on the misdemeanor, contending that the subsequent prosecution was barred by 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 110, as the dismissal of the summary offense was tantamount to an acquittal. The motion was denied, and appellant sought review. Despite notice of the appeal, the trial court found appellant guilty of the misdemeanor. On appeal, the court affirmed the denial of appellant's motion to quash. The court held that the discharge of the summary offense was not tantamount to an acquittal because there was never a prosecution that resulted in a finding of not guilty or a determination that there was insufficient evidence to warrant a conviction and that, therefore, § 110 was inapplicable. However, the court reversed appellant's conviction and remanded because the trial court lacked jurisdiction to proceed to trial once it received notice of the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant's motion to quash because the discharge of the summary offense was not tantamount to an acquittal because there was never a prosecution that resulted in a finding of not guilty and thus the bar against successive prosecutions was inapplicable. Appellant's conviction was reversed and remanded because the trial court lacked jurisdiction to proceed once it received notice of the appeal.

 

549 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Clipper


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


303 Pa. Super. 385; 449 A.2d 741; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 5040


January 28, 1981, Submitted  
August 20, 1982, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 1043 Philadelphia, 1980, Appeal from the judgment of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Lycoming County, Criminal Division, No. 79-10,301.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Lycoming County (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of retail theft, third or subsequent offense, under the Crimes Code, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3929(a)(1) and (b)(1)(IV) (1983), increasing the grade of the offense due to prior convictions for shoplifting under the Pa. Penal Code § 816.1.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of retail theft, third or subsequent offense, under the Crimes Code, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3929(a)(1) and (b)(1)(IV) (1983), and the trial court used his prior convictions for shoplifting under the Pa. Penal Code § 816.1 to increase the grade of the offense. The court vacated the conviction, holding that under the retail theft statute, § 3929(b), shoplifting convictions under the 1939 Penal Code were inapplicable to increase the grade of offense. The court found there was no legislative intent to include shoplifting under the 1939 Penal Code within the meaning of "retail theft" in § 3929(b), even though the definitions of the crimes were similar, where the statute failed to expressly include them. The court concluded that only prior retail theft convictions under the Crimes Code were intended to increase the grade of a retail theft offense under § 3929(b). Because in this case only prior shoplifting offenses under the 1939 Penal Code were introduced to increase the grade of appellant's offense, the court vacated his conviction and remanded for resentencing on retail theft as a summary offense under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3929(b)(1)(I) (1983).


OUTCOME: The court vacated the conviction and remanded for resentencing because only prior retail theft convictions were to be used to increase the grade of a retail theft offense, not only prior shoplifting offenses under the 1939 Penal Code.

Lohmiller v. Weidenbaugh


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


302 Pa. Super. 174; 448 A.2d 583; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4627


April 6, 1981, Argued  
July 16, 1982, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted November 1, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: NO. 1869 PHILADELPHIA, 1980, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division-Equity, of Montgomery County, at No. 77-10812.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife sought review of an order by the Court of Common Pleas, Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which directed that a 40 percent undivided interest in real property owned by appellant and appellee husband be partitioned. Appellant contended that the Act of May 10, 1927, 68 P.S. § 501, under which the property was to be partitioned, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellee husband's mother transferred to appellee and appellant wife, as entireties property, a total undivided interest of 40 percent in her farm. After appellee and appellant were divorced, appellee filed a complaint that sought to partition the entireties property. The trial court ordered that the 40 percent interest be partitioned. The court affirmed. The court held that the Act of May 10, 1927, 68 P.S. § 503, under which the property was to be partitioned, was not unconstitutional because it treated divorced tenants in common differently from other tenants in common. The court stated that the legislature could accord to people placed into different classes different treatment as long as the basis for the different treatment was related to the objective of the statute. The court stated that such classification had to be reasonable and rest on a distinction that had a fair and substantial relationship to the objet of the legislation. The court held that the Act's purpose was to provide for a ready, uncomplicated method of achieving some sense of economic justice upon dissolution of a marriage. The court found that the Act was a reasonable method of achieving such purpose.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which directed that a 40 percent undivided interest in real property owned by appellee husband and appellant wife be partitioned. The court stated that the legislature could accord to people placed into different classes different treatment as long as the basis for the different treatment was related to the objective of the statute.

PRIOR HISTORY: No. 2361 Philadelphia, 1980, Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division of Delaware County, at No. 1123 - 1978.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant doctor appealed a judgment of sentence for violations of the Controlled Substance, Drug, Device and Cosmetic Act, 35 P.S. § 780-101 et seq., by the Court of Common Pleas, Delaware County (Pennsylvania). Defendant argued that the trial court erred in not suppressing evidence seized under overbroad search warrants that violated his rights under U.S. Const. amend. IV.


OVERVIEW: Defendant doctor was sentenced for violations of the Controlled Substance, Drug, Device and Cosmetic Act, 35 P.S. § 780-101, et seq., after police searched his home and his office and seized his records. Defendant claimed that the two warrants were overbroad in describing the items to be seized, and therefore violated his rights under U.S. Const. amend. IV. The court reversed the trial court's judgment and granted a new trial. The court held that its examination of the warrants and the affidavits demonstrated that the warrants authorized a far broader search than was justified by the probable cause. The executing officers seized some 3,600 files, but only 50 of them were introduced in evidence at trial. The court stated that this was the kind of investigatory dragnet that the Fourth Amendment was designed to prevent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment of sentence that defendant doctor had violated the Controlled Substance, Drug, Device and Cosmetic Act. The court held that the search warrants for defendant's home and office were overbroad in describing the items to be seized, and therefore violated defendant's Fourth Amendment rights.

Commonwealth v. Dell

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] NO. 182 MARCH TERM, 1979, Appeal from the judgment of sentence in the Court of Common Pleas of York County, No. 1138 CA, 1978.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Court of Common Pleas of York County (Pennsylvania), which found him guilty of homicide by vehicle and failing to stop at a stop sign, in violation of 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 3732 and 3323(b), from which he was sentenced to from 6 to 18 months incarceration.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of homicide by vehicle, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3732, and failing to stop at a stop sign, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3323(b). Defendant was sentenced to from 6 to 18 months in prison, and he appealed his sentence. The court affirmed defendant's sentence. The court rejected defendant's claim that the homicide by vehicle statute was unconstitutional because it presented the possibility of a prison term without a finding of culpability. The court noted that under the crime of homicide by vehicle, the commonwealth was required to show only that defendant knew, or should have known, that he engaged in the conduct claimed to be in violation of § 3732, and that, at the very least, death was a probable consequence of the conduct. Therefore, the court held that § 3732 was constitutional, and defendant's conviction and sentence resulting therefrom was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the sentence entered by the lower court pursuant for defendant's convictions for homicide by vehicle and failing to stop at a stop sign. The court held that the homicide by vehicle statute was constitutional and that it only required a showing that defendant knew, or should have known, that he engaged in the conduct claimed to be in violation of the law, and that death was a probable consequence of the conduct.

Dunlap v. Philadelphia Newspapers, Inc.


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


301 Pa. Super. 475; 448 A.2d 6; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4541; 8 Media L. Rep. 1974


November 6, 1981, Argued  
July 2, 1982, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied September 30, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 115 Philadelphia, 1981, Appeal from the Order and Judgment of the Court of Common Pleas, Civil Action - Law of Phila. County at No. 4348 Nov. Term 1971.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant newspaper sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which denied its motion for a new trial or judgment n. o. v., in appellee police officer's defamation action. The trial court entered judgment in favor of appellee and the jury awarded him punitive and compensatory damages.


OVERVIEW: Appellant newspaper published a series of stories and photographs about police corruption. One photograph and story purported to be about appellee police officer. Appellee filed a defamation action against appellant, and the trial court awarded appellee compensatory and punitive damages, but denied appellant's motion for a new trial or judgment n. o. v. Appellant sought review. On appeal, the court reversed the order of the trial court because it found that the judgment n. o. v. should have been granted. The court agreed that appellee was a public figure and that the action should have been interpreted under the standard from New York Times Co. v. Sullivan. The court concluded that falsity in the publication could have been made by inferences drawn from the combination of the article, photographs and headlines. The court found that appellee had failed to prove that appellant acted with actual malice when it published that story. The reporters had not acted with reckless disregard for the truth, and had attempted to verify all their facts before publication, including verification that appellee was in the police car in the published photograph.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court which denied appellant newspaper's motion for a new trial or judgment n. o. v. The court found that appellee police officer had failed to prove that appellant acted with actual malice when it published a story and photographs about police corruption and identified appellee as the police officer in the car in the photograph.

 

556 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Hummel v. Smith


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


301 Pa. Super. 276; 447 A.2d 965; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4544


December 15, 1981, Argued  
July 2, 1982, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 505 Philadelphia, 1981, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Domestic Relations Section, of Lebanon County at No. 1483 of 1980.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of an order entered by the Court of Common Pleas of Lebanon County (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee putative father judgment on the pleadings because the trial court found that appellant's paternity action was barred by the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: Appellant mother filed a complaint against appellee putative father, which alleged that he was the father of her son, more than six years after the child's birth. The complaint also alleged that appellee had provided funds for the purchase of a bicycle and that her son had also received money from appellee on his most recent birthday. The trial court granted appellee's motion for judgment on the pleading because it found that the action was barred by the statute of limitations. On appeal, that order was reversed. Under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 6704(e), all paternity actions had to be filed within six years of a child's birth, unless the putative father had voluntarily contributed support. In that case, the matter had to be commenced within two years of the receipt of the support. However, the circumstances that surrounded any contribution had to establish that it amounted to an acknowledgement of paternity. Under the former statute, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 4323(b), which was replaced by § 6704(e), a single contribution of $ 10 had been held sufficient to meet this burden. Thus, the complaint's allegations were sufficient to defeat a motion for judgment on the pleadings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, which granted appellee putative father judgment on the pleadings in appellant mother's paternity action, and held that appellant's paternity action was not barred by the statute of limitations if she was able to establish that funds provided by appellant constituted an acknowledgement of paternity by him.

 

557 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Keeler


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


302 Pa. Super. 324; 448 A.2d 1064; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4564


March 18, 1981, Argued  
July 2, 1982, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] NO. 625 & 907 PITTSBURGH, 1980, Appeal from the order and judgments of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Mercer County, 305 Criminal 1979, and Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Mercer County, 416 Criminal 1979


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Mercer County (Pennsylvania) convicting him of criminal attempt to commit rape and indecent assault and simple assault by a prisoner. The trial court denied appellant's motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of criminal attempt to commit rape and indecent assault in one case, and in another was convicted of simple assault by a prisoner. Both cases were consolidated for appeal. The court affirmed appellant's sentence for the simple assault charge because the term was within the statutory limits. The court held that there was no evidence of actual prejudice nor was the pre-trial publicity so extensive that it justified a presumption of prejudice. It was not error for the trial court to have denied appellant's motion for change of venue. The court found that appellee commonwealth had violated Pa. R. Crim. P. 305b(1)(b) when it did not turn over inculpatory evidence to appellant. The trial court's remedy, which allowed appellant a suppression hearing, was adequate and was not an abuse of discretion. Under Pa. R. Crim. P 305E the trial court had discretion in choosing an appropriate remedy. There was sufficient evidence that sustained the guilty verdict for attempted rape. The victim testified that appellant told he was going to rape her, pushed her down, hit her, and covered her head with a shirt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for attempted rape and indecent assault and simple assault by a prisoner. The court found that appellant's sentence on the simple assault was statutorily acceptable. There was evidence that supported the attempted rape conviction, the pre-trial publicity did not prejudice appellant, and the trial court's remedy that provided appellant with a suppression hearing was proper.

Commonwealth v. Martin


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


300 Pa. Super. 497; 446 A.2d 965; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4428


April 6, 1981, Argued  
June 11, 1982, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied January 7, 1983.


PRIOR HISTORY: NO. 1358 PHILADELPHIA, 1980, Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Montgomery County, at No. 2692-79.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas, Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which sentenced defendant to serve one to two years in prison after a jury convicted him of retail theft pursuant to 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3929.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant of retail theft under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3929. The trial court denied defendant's post-trial motions and sentenced him to serve one to two years in prison. On appeal, the court vacated the judgment and remanded the case for resentencing. The court held that the trial court erred in failing to place on the record, as required, its reasons for imposing the sentence it did. The case was remanded to afford the trial court an opportunity to resentence defendant in accordance with the sentencing code and to include a statement of reasons for the sentence imposed. The court found that § 3929, which created a presumption that any person who intentionally concealed unpurchased property intended to deprive the merchant, was not unconstitutional because it satisfied the reasonable doubt standard. The evidence clearly showed beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant removed items from the store, intending to deprive the store of it, and such intent followed beyond a reasonable doubt from defendant's behavior in concealing the items. The trial court had not erred in denying defendant's motion to dismiss because defendant had waived his right to a speedy trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that sentenced defendant to serve one to two years in prison after a jury convicted him of retail theft, because the trial court failed to state on the record its reasons for imposing defendant's sentence. The case was remanded for resentencing. The court held that the retail theft statute was constitutional, and that the evidence clearly showed defendant's intent to deprive the merchant of the items.

Commonwealth v. Pavlocak


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


299 Pa. Super. 439; 445 A.2d 834; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4166


November 11, 1980, Argued  
May 14, 1982, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 172 PITTSBURGH, 1980, Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Westmoreland County, No. 68 January Term, 1979.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a ruling from the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Westmoreland County (Pennsylvania), which convicted appellant of homicide by vehicle and sentenced her to imprisonment for a period of 6 to 12 months.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted appellant of homicide by vehicle. Subsequently, the lower court denied appellant's motions for a new trial and in arrest of judgment. Thereafter, appellant was sentenced to imprisonment for a period of 6 to 12 months. Appellant sought review, claiming that the Pennsylvania Motor Vehicle Code, 75 Pa. Cons. § 3732 was unconstitutional. Further, appellant claimed that the lower court erred by interrogating her at the sentencing hearing concerning the assertion of her constitutional right to remain silent, and to thereafter rely on her silence as the basis of its sentence of imprisonment. The court affirmed the conviction, but remanded the matter for resentencing. The court found that the lower court's charge required the commonwealth to sustain a stricter burden of proof. Further, the court found that appellant was entitled to assert her privilege against self-incrimination and the lower court could not expressly penalize her for so doing. The lower court should not have relied on appellant's silence as the basis of the sentence imposed. Thus, the lower court improperly penalized appellant for asserting her constitutional right against self-incrimination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of homicide by vehicle, but remanded the matter to the jurisdiction of the lower court for resentencing. The court held that the lower court improperly penalized appellant for asserting her constitutional right against self-incrimination at the sentencing hearing.

Mancine v. Concord-Liberty Sav. & Loan Asso.


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


299 Pa. Super. 260; 445 A.2d 744; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4048


April 15, 1980, Argued  
April 30, 1982, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 853 April Term, 1979, Appeal from the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Civil Division, at GD 75-02451


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owner sought review of an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which denied her motion for a new trial after the trial court held that a confession of judgment upon a warrant of attorney after the death of the obligor made the judgment voidable as between the obligor and obligee not void.


OVERVIEW: Appellant owner instituted an action in assumpsit against appellee obligees for damages for the unlawful entry of judgment, wrongful, malicious, and fraudulent dispossession of appellant from her home, loss of her belongings, for the rental value of her home, for the fair market value of her home, for the loss to appellant's reputation, and for exemplary and punitive damages. The court found that where the obligor was deceased, it automatically terminated the warrant of attorney to confess judgment. The court also found that appellant was the record owner of the property sold by the sheriff and was in possession of the property at the time of sale. Thus, appellant was entitled to damages.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, which denied appellant owner's motion for a new trial after the trial court held that a confession of judgment upon a warrant of attorney after the death of the obligor made the judgment voidable as between the obligor and obligee not void. The court reversed the judgment. The court found that the trial court erroneously ruled that the judgment was voidable and not void.

Commonwealth v. King


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


298 Pa. Super. 499; 444 A.2d 1294; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 4059


June 10, 1980, Argued  
April 30, 1982, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 2393 October Term, 1979, Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Centre County, at No. 31 of 1979.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction from the judgment of sentence by the Court of Common Pleas of Centre County, (Pennsylvania) for homicide by vehicle. Appellant filed post-verdict motions that were denied. On appeal, appellant contended the evidence was insufficient to sustain his conviction and that Vehicle Code, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3732 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of homicide by vehicle in the trial court. Appellant then filed post-verdict motions that were denied. Appellant sought review of his conviction on appeal contending insufficient evidence sustained his conviction and that 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3732, part of the Vehicle Code which discussed the elements of homicide by vehicle, was unconstitutional. The court found § 3732, part of the Vehicle Code, was a first-degree misdemeanor that did not use ambiguous words, archaic classification, or words with varied meanings. Therefore, § 3732 was constitutional. The court also concluded the evidence supported appellant's conviction where testimony presented was that appellant made a statement to a trooper that he was driving too fast and lost control of his vehicle. It was also established that one passenger was killed in the accident when his body was thrown an additional 69 feet after the vehicle appellant drove had been airborne after going off an embankment. The court affirmed the trial court judgment convicting appellant of homicide by vehicle.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment against appellant for homicide by vehicle. The court found the homicide by vehicle provision in the Vehicle Law was a first-degree misdemeanor that did not use ambiguous words, archaic classification, or words with varied meanings, and was constitutional. The court also concluded evidence supported appellant's conviction where one passenger died and appellant admitted he lost control of his vehicle.

 

562 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Dragun v. Volk


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


301 Pa. Super. 443; 447 A.2d 1381; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3964


March 17, 1981, Argued  
April 23, 1982, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument Denied August 6, 1982. Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted September 13, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 968 Pittsburgh, 1980, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, Allegheny County, at No. GD 78-3933


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, injured persons, challenged the order from the Court of Common Pleas, Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) that granted the motion of defendants, tortfeasors, for summary judgment on plaintiffs' claim for noneconomic damages under the Pennsylvania No Fault Motor Vehicle Act, 40 P.S. §§ 1009.101-1009.701. Appellants claimed that therapy costs were not excluded from the $ 750 threshold of 40 P.S. § 1009.301(a)(5)(B).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, husband and wife, were injured in a car accident with defendants, husband and wife tortfeasors, and sued for noneconomic damages under the Pennsylvania No Fault Motor Vehicle Act (Act), 40 P.S. §§ 1009.101-1009.701. The trial court granted defendants' motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court held that under 40 P.S. § 1009.301(a)(5)(B), defendants were not liable unless appellants' medical bills exceeded $ 750, but that diagnostic X-rays and rehabilitation costs in excess of $ 100 were not included in calculating the $ 750 threshold. After examining the purposes and definitions of the Act in 40 P.S. §§ 1009.102 and 1009.103, the court held that plaintiff wife's dynamic cerebral was a diagnostic tool using X-rays, and that plaintiff wife's physical therapy was for rehabilitation because it was not part of the treatment from an independent practicing professional, or part of her professional nursing care or hospitalization. Thus, the dynamic cerebral and physical therapy costs over $ 100 was excluded. Therefore, because plaintiffs' expenses were below the §750 threshold, defendants were entitled to summary judgment and the court affirmed the order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting the motion of defendants, tortfeasors, for summary judgment on the claim of plaintiffs, injured persons, for noneconomic damages under the Pennsylvania No Fault Motor Vehicle Act (Act). The court held that because plaintiffs could not include dynamic cerebral and therapy costs over $ 100 in calculating their medical costs, plaintiffs' costs were less than $ 750 and defendants were not liable under the Act.

 

563 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Walker


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


298 Pa. Super. 387; 444 A.2d 1228; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3995


October 19, 1981, Submitted  
April 23, 1982, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 2242 Philadelphia, 1980, Appeal from judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas, Trial Division, Criminal Section of the County of Philadelphia at Nos. 1992, 1995, 1996, 1998-2020, 2027-2040, 2049-2132, 2136-2176, September Term, 1979


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas, County of Philadelphia (Pennsylvania) which convicted him pursuant to Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 18, §§ 903(a) and 4701(a)(3) of multiple counts of criminal conspiracy and bribery in connection with his former public employment, and imposed two concurrent sentences of six to 23 months incarceration.


OVERVIEW: While a municipal employee, appellant accepted payment for facilitating the unlawful dumping of chemical wastes in city landfills. He was convicted of multiple counts of criminal conspiracy under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 903(a) and bribery under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 18, § 4701(a)(3). The trial court sentenced appellant to two concurrent terms of six to 23 months incarceration. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of sentence. Appellant's prosecution was not time barred, the court held, because Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 18, § 108(c)(2) extended three years to the underlying statute of limitations where the offense was committed by a public employee in connection with his employment. The court rejected appellant's challenge to the bribery statute, § 4701(a)(3), finding that its prohibition against a public servant's contravention of a "known legal duty" was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to appellant. Despite instructions from his supervisor, the court noted, appellant not only allowed the unlawful activity for remuneration, but also used a bulldozer to cover the wastes and shared his dishonest profits with other city employees to prevent their reporting the illegal dumpings.


OUTCOME: Finding that appellant's prosecution was timely and rejecting his constitutional challenge to the bribery statute, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting appellant of multiple counts of bribery and criminal conspiracy and sentencing him to incarceration.

 

564 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Koch


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


297 Pa. Super. 350; 443 A.2d 1157; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3806


June 25, 1981, Argued  
April 2, 1982, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied July 1, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 1626 Philadelphia, 1980, Appeal from Judgment of Sentence in the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Lancaster County, at No. 1018 of 1979.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Lancaster County (Pennsylvania), which convicted defendant of homicide by vehicle in violation of 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3732.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered an intersection and collided with another vehicle, killing one of the passengers. Defendant contended that 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3732 was unconstitutional because it constituted a violation of due process and was a strict liability statute. The court affirmed defendant's conviction for homicide by vehicle. 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3732 was not a strict liability statute and was not unconstitutional. 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3732 required a showing that defendant deviated from the standard of care established by the underlying Vehicle Code provision. The Commonwealth was also required to prove that defendant's violation of the underlying Vehicle Code provision caused the victim's death. The requirement that defendant knew, or should have known, that he was violating the underlying Vehicle Code provision established some kind of culpability on his part and precluded 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3732 from being a strict liability statute. There was no requirement that the Commonwealth file a separate complaint alleging the particular Vehicle Code violation. Defendant was given adequate warning of such violation in the complaint.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for homicide by vehicle. The homicide by vehicle statute was not a strict liability statute and was not unconstitutional because the Commonwealth was required to prove that defendant violated a Vehicle Code provision and that the violation led to a death. The Commonwealth was not required to file a separate complaint alleging the particular Vehicle Code provision.

Crisante v. J. H. Beers, Inc.


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


297 Pa. Super. 337; 443 A.2d 1150; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3807


December 4, 1980, Argued  
April 2, 1982, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied July 14, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 1665 Philadelphia, 1980, Appeal from Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, of Northampton County at No. 1979-C-13162.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of a judgment from the Court of Common Pleas of Northampton County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed appellant's complaint that alleged that appellee construction contractor's negligent operation of its equipment caused excessive vibrations and resulted in damage to appellant's residence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant landowner's negligence complaint against appellee construction contractor was dismissed because it was barred by the two-year statute of limitations. Appellant argued that 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5524(4) did not apply to actions that alleged only negligence. Rather, appellant argued that 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5527(6) applied to this action and thus, the action was not barred by the two-year statute of limitations. The court affirmed and held that causes of action alleging negligent infliction of damage to real property were governed by § 5524(4). Thus, because appellant's action alleged negligence and was governed by § 5524(4), her action was barred by the two-year statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of appellant landowner's complaint against appellee construction contractor. The court held that the two-year statute of limitations applied to negligence actions such as appellant's action and therefore, the trial court properly dismissed appellant's action as untimely.

Commonwealth v. Porta


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


297 Pa. Super. 298; 443 A.2d 845; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3768


November 5, 1981, Submitted  
March 26, 1982, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied September 1, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 381 Philadelphia, 1981, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Pennsylvania, Criminal Division at Nos. 367-368 January Term, 1954.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which denied his request for relief under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 1965 Pa. Laws 1580, § 1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to first-degree murder. The trial court imposed a sentence of life imprisonment after accepting appellant's plea. Appellant took neither a direct appeal from the judgment entered nor did he submit a petition to withdraw his plea. Instead, he filed a pro se petition for relief under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act (PCHA), 1965 Pa. Laws 1580, § 1 et seq, alleging the denial of his right to the representation by competent counsel at the preliminary hearing. The trial court denied the petition, and appellant sought review. The court ruled that the waiver provisions of the PCHA did not apply retroactively to bar consideration of claims that could have been raised in a direct appeal or in a habeas corpus petition prior to the PCHA's effective date, unless the petitioner knowingly and understandingly failed to raise the claim. Hence, the court ruled that the waiver concept did not bar appellant's claim. Nevertheless, the court affirmed the trial court because its findings were supported in the record.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the trial court order denying appellant's request for relief under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act. The court ruled that appellant was not entitled to relief because the trial court's findings were supported by the evidence in the record.

Havelka v. Sheraskey


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


295 Pa. Super. 326; 441 A.2d 1255; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3430


September 2, 1981, Argued  
February 19, 1982, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 299 Pittsburgh, 1981, Appeal from the Judgment of the Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, of Washington County at No. 461 May Term 1979, A.D.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, Washington County, Pennsylvania, which assessed delay damages against him after a jury verdict in a personal injury suit brought by appellee injured party.


OVERVIEW: Appellant driver was operating a vehicle that struck appellee injured party, who was trying to push a disabled car, causing appellee serious injury. Appellee filed suit, and the jury rendered a verdict against appellant. The trial court then assessed delay damages against appellant pursuant to Pa. R. Civ. P. 238, and appellant challenged this ruling on appeal. The court affirmed and held that appellant neither raised the issue of the constitutionality of Rule 238 in the trial court nor notified the court administrator of Pennsylvania of his constitutional challenge to the rule as required by Pa. R. App. P. 522. Therefore, the court held that appellant had waived the issue. The court also pointed out that the Pennsylvania Supreme Court had already found Rule 238 constitutional and not a violation of due process or equal protection as guaranteed by the Pennsylvania and United States Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's assessment of delay damages against appellant driver in a personal injury suit brought by appellee injured party because appellant failed to raise the issue of the constitutionality of such assessment at trial and also failed to notify the court administrator of his challenge. Thus, appellant waived the issue on appeal.

Commonwealth v. Hawkins


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


295 Pa. Super. 429; 441 A.2d 1308; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3437


April 29, 1981, Argued  
February 19, 1982, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 149 Pittsburgh, 1980, Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County, Criminal Division, at No. CC 7802146A (1321 of 1978).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas of Erie County, Criminal Division (Pennsylvania), which convicted him of theft by deception, receiving stolen property, misapplication of government property, tampering with witnesses, and criminal conspiracy.


OVERVIEW: The lower court convicted defendant of theft by deception, receiving stolen property, misapplication of government property, tampering with witnesses, and criminal conspiracy. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the lower court did not err in denying defendant's motion to dismiss the charges because 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 108(c)(2) (repealed) provided an exception to the statute of limitations whenever the public officer or employee had continuously occupied any office or employment. The lower court did not err in admitting evidence of other crimes as there was no prejudice. The lower court properly instructed the jury not to consider the consequences to defendant if they returned a guilty verdict. The jury charge covered the requested point regarding other alleged accomplice-witnesses. The trial court did not err in refusing to charge the jury that lack of force was not an element of the misdemeanor of witness tampering because the instruction would have created confusion. The trial court's procedure in reading to the jury the statutory definition of misapplication of government property was sufficient to place the issue of intent properly before the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and held that the prosecution was timely commenced under an exception to the statute of limitations, the trial court properly admitted evidence of other crimes as there was no prejudice to defendant, and the trial court's jury instructions were proper.
