Samsel v. Travelers Indem. Co.


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


295 Pa. Super. 188; 441 A.2d 412; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3465


December 2, 1980, Argued  
February 5, 1982, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied May 6, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: NO. 989 PHILADELPHIA, 1980, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Civil Action-Law, of Luzerne County, at No. 3774 of 1979


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant motorcycle operator challenged a decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Luzerne County (Pennsylvania), which excluded him from insurance coverage under the Pennsylvania No-Fault Motor Vehicle Insurance Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 40, § 1009 et seq., when he was injured in an collision with an automobile.

Further, the exclusionary provisions of the Act had been held constitutional by the Pennsylvania Supreme Court because of the greater risk of serious injury to the operator or passenger of a motorcycle and the resulting increase in No-Fault insurance premiums if such person were to be included.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court was affirmed.

Mattia v. Employers Mut. Cos.


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


294 Pa. Super. 577; 440 A.2d 616; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3282


April 1, 1981, Argued  
January 29, 1982, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 2650 Philadelphia, 1980, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, Philadelphia County, at No. 2996 November Term, 1978.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, injured, challenged the decision of the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee insurance company's motion for summary judgment in a suit to collect under the Pennsylvania No-fault Motor Vehicle Insurance Act, 40 P. S. §§ 1009.101 et seq. Appellees claimed that the act precluded her recovery of work loss benefits because she was self employed and showed no income at the time of the injury.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, injured, was crossing the street on foot when an automobile struck her. Appellee insurance company refused to compensate appellant under the Pennsylvania No-fault Motor Vehicle Insurance Act (Act), 40 P. S. §§ 1009.101 et seq., claiming that §202(b) and § 205 of the Act precluded her recovery of work loss benefits. Appellant, a self-employed florist and had shown no income in her newly opened business. The court held that strict application of the formula set forth in § 205(a) did not permit appellant to recoup a reasonable amount of work loss, and caused an absurd and unreasonable result. The court held that insurance statutes were not designated by the legislature as requiring strict construction. The court held that in suffering a deficit from her newly opened business appellant was an individual "who has not previously earned income from work." The court reversed and remanded holding that her probable income could have been determined in accordance with the formula appearing in § 205(d), subsection (c). Thus, the question of appellant's work loss benefits should have gone to the jury as a triable issue of fact, and the granting of a summary judgment was incorrect.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the lower court and remanded the case for proceedings because a doubt as to a triable issue of material fact existed, and appellant's probable income could have been determined in accordance with the formula appearing in the Act.

Long v. 130 Market Street Gift & Novelty


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


294 Pa. Super. 383; 440 A.2d 517; 1982 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3167


April 9, 1979, Argued  
January 14, 1982, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 1107 April Term, 1978, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, Cambria County, at No. 1978-1169.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, individuals and business, challenged the judgment of the Court of Common Pleas, Cambria County (Pennsylvania) that permanently enjoined appellants from selling or distributing certain publications and films which a jury determined to be obscene within the definition of the anti-obscenity statute.


OVERVIEW: Appellee District Attorney of Cambria County filed a complaint in equity under the injunction provision of the anti-obscenity statute, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5903(g) and requested that a hearing be held within three days' time. The jury returned a unanimous verdict and found that all the material before it was obscene. Appellants alleged that there was insufficient evidence to submit the matter to the jury because appellee presented no evidence concerning the community standard of the element of the offense. The court held that the materials themselves were sufficient evidence for the jury to determine whether the average person would find that the materials appealed to prurient interest. Appellants alleged that appellee's remarks to the jury were improper because they had inherently religious implications. The court held that any error was cured because the trial court specifically instructed the jury to ignore their personal religious and moral beliefs. Because the court modified the injunction to encompass only those materials actually found to be obscene by the jury, it did not consider appellants' allegations that the injunction was vague and overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court enjoining appellants, individuals and company, from selling or distributing the materials submitted to the jury and determined to be obscene within the definition of the anti-obscenity statute. The court amended the order to encompass only those publications and films named in the complaint and reviewed by the jury.

Gordon v. Gordon

April 23, 1981, Argued

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), denying appellant's application that her divorce action proceed under the Divorce Code of 1980, 23 Pa. Const. Stat. § 1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant brought a divorce action under the Divorce Law of 1929, 23 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1 et seq. (repealed), and it was pending when the Divorce Code of 1980, 23 Pa. Cons. Appellant filed an application for her action to proceed under the Divorce Code to take advantage of provisions allowing equitable distribution of marital property and payment of alimony after divorce. The court concluded that granting appellant's application would have furthered these objectives and advanced the policies of the commonwealth.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court denying appellant's application for her divorce action to proceed under the most recent divorce code. The court determined that application of the more recent divorce code would have effectuated economic justice.

Sachritz v. Pennsylvania Nat'l Mut. Casualty Ins. Co.


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


293 Pa. Super. 483; 439 A.2d 678; 1981 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3722


May 1, 1981, Argued  
October 30, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument Denied February 5, 1982. Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted May 26, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 1097 Pittsburgh, 1980, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Civil Division, at No. GD 79-19760.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant spouse of deceased injured insured challenged the grant of summary by the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania) in favor of appellee no-fault insurer in appellant's action to recover work loss benefits accrued after the date of her husband's death as his survivor.


OVERVIEW: Appellant spouse of deceased injured insured filed a complaint against appellee no-fault insurer for work loss benefits accrued after the date of her husband's death as his survivor. Appellee filed a motion for summary judgment alleging that the complaint was untimely filed because the applicable two year statute of limitations had expired. The trial court agreed with appellee and dismissed appellant's complaint. On appeal, appellant alleged that none of the statute of limitations contained in the Pennsylvania No-Fault Motor Vehicle Insurance Act, 40 P.S. § 1009.101et seq. (1974) applied to recover additional work loss benefits and that her action was timely commenced within the six year period allowable for contracts. The court affirmed finding that 40 P.S. § 1009.106(c)(1) provided for a two year statute of limitations for the benefits appellant claimed. The court also found that appellant was aware of her eligibility for benefits and although they were complex and possibly ambiguous it did not support a conclusion of its unconstitutionality for reasons of vagueness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of no-fault insurer in appellant spouse of deceased injured insured's action to recover work loss benefits because the applicable statute of limitations was two years not six years the allowable period for contracts.

 

575 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Pugar v. Greco


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


291 Pa. Super. 476; 436 A.2d 215; 1981 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3616


January 13, 1981, Argued  
October 23, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 412 Pittsburgh, 1980, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division of Allegheny County at No. 7356 of 1976.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver challenged an order by the Allegheny County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania), which denied his motion to quash the appeal from an arbitration award filed by appellees, car driver and car owner. Appellant claimed that appellees were forbidden from filing an appeal from arbitration because they failed to comply with Pa. R. App. P. 1701(b)(3), and, thus, their appeal was not timely filed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant driver crashed into a car that was driven by appellee car driver and was owned by appellee car owner. The arbitrators found in favor of appellant, and appellees filed a motion asking the lower court to forego payment of the appeal bond asserting that requiring payment before appeal chilled their constitutional right to a jury trial. The lower court denied the motion, and appellees then filed an appeal and bond. Appellant claimed that the filing of a motion contesting the bond amount had not tolled the time requirements in Pa. R. App. P. 1701(b)(3) and that appellees were estopped from filing the appeal. The court held that appellees were not allowed any additional time for perfecting an appeal. In addition, it said that the clock continued to run pursuant to Pa. R. App. P. 1701(b)(3) while they filed their motions. However, the court also held that the general rule was inapplicable because the motion challenged the very appeal procedure itself and not the lower court's order per se. The court reasoned that appellees' belief that once the fee was paid, they would forever lose their ability to challenge the constitutionality of the rule, was a reasonable one.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed. It concluded that appellees, car driver and car owner, could proceed with their appeal and trial de novo. The court reasoned that because appellees thought that if they paid that appeal bond they would be waiving any right to challenge it later, they were excused from strict compliance with the court rule regarding perfecting an appeal.

 

576 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Bond v. Gallen


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


292 Pa. Super. 207; 437 A.2d 7; 1981 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3527


June 25, 1981, Argued  
October 16, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted March 16, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 1087 Philadelphia, 1980, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, of Delaware County, at No. 79-5619.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant motorist sought review of an order entered by the Court of Common Pleas of Delaware County (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee driver's motion for judgment on the pleadings in appellant's action to recover damages resulting from a motor vehicle accident.


OVERVIEW: Appellant motorist was injured when appellee driver crashed his car into hers. Over two years after the accident, appellant filed suit against appellee to recover damages, including the medical expenses she incurred as a result of the accident. The trial court granted appellee's motion for judgment on the pleadings, finding that appellant's claim was barred by the two year statute of limitations of the No-fault Motor Vehicle Insurance Act (Act), 40 P.S. 1009.101 et seq., as appellant did not file suit within two years of the accident. The court reversed, concluding that the limitations period of the Act did not begin to run until the claimant knew or by the exercise of reasonable diligence should have known that one of the threshold conditions for filing suit, as set forth in § 301(a) of the Act, had been reached. The court thus remanded the matter to the trial court for consideration of whether appellant filed suit within two years after she knew or should have known that her medical expenses would exceed $ 750, which was the § 301 (a) threshold condition plaintiff sought to establish in her pleadings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting appellee driver's motion for judgment on the pleadings because the two year limitations period of the no-fault act began to run not on the date of the accident, but on the date on which appellant motorist knew or should have known that one of the threshold conditions for filing suit under the act had been reached. The court remanded the matter for consideration of whether appellant timely filed suit.

Edward M. v. O'Neill


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


291 Pa. Super. 531; 436 A.2d 628; 1981 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3547


November 16, 1979, Argued  
October 16, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied January 29, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 1502 October Term, 1979, No. 1858 October Term, 1979, No. 1859 October Term, 1979, No. 1860 October Term, 1979, Appeals from Orders of the Court of Common Pleas, Civil Division, of Philadelphia County at Nos. 3904 April, 1979, 2257-79-3 DC No. 18-79-16285 J No. 216053, 2795-79-4 DC No. 15-79-21997, J No. 172468, DC9-79 10888, J192791 2257- 79-3 DC 18-79-16285 J 216053 2795- 79-4 DC 15-79-21997 J 172468 2304-79-3 No. 3784-79-4 3778- 79-4 DC 1-79-6999 38880- 79-5 DC 19-79-31753 J1 82550 J 112294 DC 6-79-24685 6-79-2587 (SIC) 6-79-24875 J 216925 2290793.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The commonwealth filed appeals from orders of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), in which a juvenile court judge sua sponte granted an injunction to cease use of Philadelphia Police Department Directive 95 and granted motions to expunge two juvenile defendants' records, and other juveniles sought review of a judge's order, sitting in equity, which refused to enjoin the directive and grant them class certification.


OVERVIEW: This case consolidated appeals involving the legality of Philadelphia Police Department Directive 95, which directed the fingerprinting and photographing of juvenile arrestees over age 15. The commonwealth appealed a juvenile court judge's orders that granted motions to expunge two juvenile defendants' records that were made under the directive and that granted an injunction to cease use of the directive. Other juveniles sought review of a judge's order, sitting in equity, which refused to enjoin the directive and grant them class certification. After the appeals were filed, legislation was enacted that specifically authorized the fingerprinting and photographing of juveniles. The court found that the appeals were not entirely moot and reversed the sua sponte injunction order because it effected class-wide relief after the lower court properly denied class certification. The court also reversed the expungement order because that remedy was not available to the two juvenile defendants who were adjudicated delinquent. The court affirmed the order that denied the injunction and refused class certification because the cases were fact-specific and did not represent a class.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the juvenile court's orders that enjoined the police directive and expunged records made under it, and concluded that the injunction improperly mandated class-wide relief after class certification was denied, and that expungement was not available to juveniles who were found delinquent. The court affirmed the order that denied class certification and injunctive relief because the cases did not represent a class of arrestees.

Bianco v. Concepts "100", Inc.


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


291 Pa. Super. 458; 436 A.2d 206; 1981 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3566


December 4, 1980, Argued  
October 9, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied January 26, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 1233 Philadelphia, 1980, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Civil Division, at No. 2033 January Term, 1977.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judgment creditor sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which sustained appellee garnishee's objections to jurisdiction in appellant's attachment execution proceedings on the ground that it lacked jurisdiction over appellee because the garnishment proceedings were in rem in nature, and appellee did not have property within the territorial reach of Pennsylvania process.


OVERVIEW: Appellant judgment creditor obtained a judgment against a New York corporation that was insured by appellee garnishee, although appellee had disclaimed coverage for appellant's cause of action. Appellant filed a writ of execution and interrogatories in attachment against appellee as garnishee. Appellee filed preliminary objections to the interrogatories, which asserted that the lower court lacked jurisdiction. The lower court sustained appellee's objections, and reasoned that, although appellee was subject to in personam jurisdiction, Pennsylvania courts lacked jurisdiction in the garnishment proceedings because they were in rem in nature, and appellee had no property within the territorial reach of Pennsylvania process. Appellant sought review, and the court reversed, remanded, and concluded that appellee was subject to garnishment in Pennsylvania. The lower court erred when it applied principles of in rem jurisdiction because, pursuant to 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 5301(a)(2), (b) and 40 P.S. § 421, the insured was a foreign insurance corporation that was authorized to do business in the commonwealth and voluntarily subjected itself to the courts' jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's order, which sustained appellee garnishee's objections to jurisdiction in appellant judgment creditor's attachment execution action, remanded, and concluded that the insured was subject to the jurisdiction of Pennsylvania courts because it was a foreign insurance corporation that was authorized to do business in the commonwealth, and the lower court erred when it applied the principles of in rem jurisdiction.

Hamay v. County of Washington


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


291 Pa. Super. 137; 435 A.2d 606; 1981 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3427


April 16, 1980, Submitted  
September 25, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 687 April Term, 1979, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Washington County, Civil Division, at No. 135 August Term, 1978 A.D.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant confinee sought review of the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Washington County, Civil Division (Pennsylvania), granting summary judgment to appellee county on appellant's claim of illegal arrest and confinement. Appellant had failed to comply with his support obligations, owing to reduced income, and a bench warrant was issued leading to his arrest and subsequent confinement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant confinee failed to comply with his support obligations. A bench warrant was issued and appellant was arrested. Appellant sought review of the trial court's decision granting summary judgment to appellee county on his claim of illegal arrest and confinement. The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment, finding that it had not abused its discretion in refusing to grant appellant's request to change venue because judicial impartiality was not necessarily compromised where a trial court judge was a judge in a county being sued. The court also found that appellant had no respondeat superior claim against appellee based on a judge's actions because the judge was an employee of the commonwealth of Pennsylvania, not of the county. Similarly, the court found that county employees such as the sheriff and his deputies could not have committed a tort unless they were ordered by a judge who had been acting without jurisdiction, which was not the case. Alternatively, the court found that appellant could not proceed on the merits of the case because he had failed to properly appeal his claim that the statute under which he was arrested was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment, holding that the trial court had not erred in not changing venue because judicial impartiality was not necessarily compromised where a trial court judge was a judge in a county being sued. The court also found that appellant confinee had no respondeat superior claim against appellee county based on a judge's actions and that he had failed to properly appeal the constitutionality of a statute he challenged.

OVERVIEW: Appellant minor was injured in an automobile accident. Two years and four months later, while appellant was still a minor, suit was brought in her name. United States Fidelity & Guaranty Co. v. United Farm Bureau Mut. Ins. Co.


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


297 Pa. Super. 25; 443 A.2d 280; 1981 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3373


March 18, 1981, Argued  
September 4, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument Denied April 13, 1982. Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted November 5, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 758 Pittsburgh, 1980, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Civil Division, at No. GD 80-5285


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nonresident insurer sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), denying appellant's preliminary objections regarding assumption of personal jurisdiction over appellant in appellee insurance administrator's declaratory judgment action seeking a ruling that appellant owed benefits to appellee insureds arising out of an automobile accident which occurred in Pennsylvania.


OVERVIEW: Appellee, an insurance company which was assigned to administer claims filed by appellee insureds pursuant to the assigned claims plan of the Pennsylvania No-Fault Motor Vehicle Insurance Act, brought a declaratory judgment action seeking a ruling that appellant nonresident insurer owed benefits to appellee insureds arising out of an automobile accident which occurred in Pennsylvania. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying appellant insurer's preliminary objections regarding assumption of personal jurisdiction because the due process requirements were satisfied where appellant had clear notice that it was subject to being involved in suits in Pennsylvania by agreeing to cover appellee insureds' losses incurred while operating their automobile and by requiring a cooperative effort in litigation.

Commonwealth ex rel. Grimes v. Yack


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


289 Pa. Super. 495; 433 A.2d 1363; 1981 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3294


August 10, 1981, Argued  
August 21, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied October 26, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 537 Philadelphia, 1981, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Northampton County at No. 1980-C-8916.

No. 1806 Philadelphia, 1981, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Northampton County at No. 8916 of 1980.

No. 1481 Philadelphia, 1981, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adoptive parents sought review from the Court of Common Pleas of Northampton County and the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County (Pennsylvania), which consolidated an adoption cause of action and ordered that appellants return the child to appellee natural parents, pursuant to the Adoption Act, 1 P.S. § 101, et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant adoptive parents obtained possession of a child with the intent of adopting her. Appellee natural parents changed their minds about consenting to such adoption. The trial courts held that, as an adoption case, the only issue was whether the record indicated any reason why appellees' interests as mother and father of the child should have been involuntarily terminated. In a consolidated action from two separate trial courts, it was determined that no such reason existed, and appellants were ordered to return the child to appellees. Pursuant to the Adoption Act, 1 P.S. § 414, consent to an adoption was required of parents of an adoptee who had not reached the age of 18 years. Consent of the parents was not required if a decree of termination with regard to such parents had been entered. The court held that consent to an adoption by the natural parents could have been withdrawn at any time before entry of the final decree of adoption. The court held that appellees' rights could not have been involuntarily terminated pursuant to the Adoption Act, 1 P.S. § 311. The court affirmed orders of the trial courts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed orders of the trial courts, which ordered appellant adoptive parents to return the child to appellee natural parents. Pursuant to the Adoption Act, the court held that appellees could have withdrawn their consent to an adoption at any time before the entry of the final decree of adoption. The court held that appellees' rights could not have been involuntarily terminated.

Commonwealth v. Wright


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


289 Pa. Super. 399; 433 A.2d 511; 1981 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3210


January 7, 1981, Argued  
August 7, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied January 11, 1982.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 1616 Philadelphia, 1980, Appeal from Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, of Cumberland County, No. 996 of 1979.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of sentence from the Court of Common Pleas of Cumberland County (Pennsylvania), which found appellant guilty of willful non-support of his minor son. Post-trial motions had been denied, and appellant was sentenced to prison for not less than 6 nor more than 12 months.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of willful non-support of his minor son. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of sentence and held that the evidence was sufficient to enable the fact finder to infer a willful refusal by appellant to support his son due to the fact that appellant had worked during the period that he did not make support payments. The court also held that the officer's destruction of his notes was not a suppression of the evidence by the commonwealth and did not render his testimony incompetent. The notes were used to produce an office memorandum, which the officer could have used to refresh his recollection, and which was made available for inspection by defense counsel. The court also held that the statute appellant was charged under, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 18, § 4321(a), was not violative of the Equal Rights Amendment of the state constitution, Pa. Const. art. I, § 28. Under Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 1, § 2301(a), where statutes were enacted where there was a designation restricted to a single sex, the references to a single sex was deemed applicable to both sexes. Thus, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 18, § 4321(a) applied to both parents, and appellant's argument failed.


OUTCOME: The court held that the evidence was sufficient to enable the fact finder to infer a willful refusal by appellant to support his son. The court also held that the destruction of preliminary notes went to the credibility of the officer's testimony, and not to its admissibility. Finally, the court held that the statute that appellant was charged with was not violative of the Equal Rights Amendment of the state constitution.

Commonwealth v. Dodge


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


287 Pa. Super. 148; 429 A.2d 1143; 1981 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2673


November 12, 1980, Argued  
May 15, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied August 24, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 969 April Term, 1979, Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County, Criminal Division at No. CC7803903A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), for prostitution under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5902(a) and criminal conspiracy under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 903(a)(1). The trial court denied defendant's petition for a mistrial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of prostitution, under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5902(a), and criminal conspiracy under 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 903(a)(1). On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment and disposed of several of her allegations regarding the constitutionality of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5902 because of lack of standing. She was charged with violating 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5902(a)(1) in that she engaged in sexual activity as a business, and thus only had standing to object to the constitutionality of that section. She did have standing to argue that the term "sexual activity as a business" in § 5902(a)(1) was too vague, but the court found no merit in the argument, because it provided a person of ordinary intelligence with fair notice of the type of conduct proscribed. The court held that § 5902(a) did not violate defendant's right to privacy, as the proscribed activity was a commercial activity, and that the statute was rationally related to a valid state interest. Where an officer's statement regarding investigating criminal activities did not give the jury any basis for inferring that he had investigated defendant on a prior date, the motion for the mistrial was correctly denied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of sentence for prostitution and criminal conspiracy. The court concluded that all the state was required to show was that the prohibition of prostitution was rationally related to a valid state interest, as it did not affect defendant's right to privacy. Defendant's motion for a mistrial was properly denied, and as there was not basis for the jury to infer that appellant had engaged in prior criminal activity.

Commonwealth v. Green

OVERVIEW: The trial court entered a judgment sentence against defendant after he was convicted by a jury of making terroristic threats in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 2706. In Interest of Jones


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


286 Pa. Super. 574; 429 A.2d 671; 1981 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2621


November 13, 1979, Argued  
May 8, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 123 April Term, 1979, Appeal from an Order of the Court of Common Pleas, Family Division, of Allegheny County, Juvenile Section, No. J-310-1976.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which denied appellant custody of her two adjudicated dependent children.


OVERVIEW: Appellant mother's two children were adjudicated dependent pursuant to a petition by the Child Welfare Services and were removed from her custody. Both girls were placed with their maternal aunt and appellant continued to maintain regular contact with the children. After she underwent psychiatric care and counseling appellant filed a petition for a hearing to regain custody. The lower court denied the petition based on testimony from an unidentified witness about appellant's relationship with a same-sex partner. Appellant sought review, alleging that she was denied the right to confront the witness. On appeal, the court reversed the lower court's decision because appellant was deprived of due process by the admission of hearsay into evidence. The court found that the information furnished by the unidentified witness was critical to the court's final determination and appellant should have been afforded an opportunity to confront the witness. The court held that a portion of 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 6341(d) was unconstitutional because it allowed testimony into evidence regardless of whether there was an opportunity provided to test the veracity and reliability of the declarant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the lower court's order denying appellant mother custody of her children who where adjudicated dependants. The court held that the lower court's decision failed to provide appellant with due process because the order was based on hearsay testimony from an undisclosed witness.

 

588 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Spurgeon


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


285 Pa. Super. 563; 428 A.2d 189; 1981 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2414


December 1, 1980, Argued  
April 3, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied May 5, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 395 Phila., 1980, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County indexed at No. 3636-79.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which dismissed his pretrial motion to quash criminal informations. He argued that, because the trial court had dismissed a summary charge due to the Commonwealth's failure to make a prima facie case, double jeopardy, and/or collateral estoppel, and/or 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 110 barred his prosecution on other charges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the order of the trial court, which dismissed his pretrial motion to quash criminal informations. On appeal, the court held that the trial court's dismissal of a reckless driving charge constituted an acquittal. However, under 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3732, reckless driving was not a necessary element of the crime of homicide by vehicle. The second element of that offense was met if it was established that defendant violated any law of the Commonwealth or municipal ordinance pertaining to the use of a vehicle or to the regulation of traffic. Proving a speeding charge against defendant would not involve relitigation of the reckless driving charge, so neither double jeopardy nor collateral estoppel barred the prosecution. Section 3732 did not require a showing of reckless or negligent culpability on defendant's part in order to sustain a conviction. Because the other offenses with which defendant was charged required proof of facts not common to reckless driving and each offense was designed to prevent a substantially different harm or evil, neither 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 110, nor a case decided under that statute, barred the prosecutions. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to quash. The dismissal of the reckless driving offense constituted an acquittal on that charge. However, reckless driving was not an element of the crime of homicide by vehicle, so neither double jeopardy nor collateral estoppel barred those prosecutions. Defendant's other charges required proof of different facts not common to reckless driving, so the statute did not bar the prosecutions.

The statute under which appellant was convicted was sufficiently informative to comply with constitutional notice requirements, the evidence of victims' terror was sufficient, and admission of evidence of appellant's silence after arrest was not improper, but assuming it was, the curative instruction protected appellant's interest.

Commonwealth v. Thomas


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


284 Pa. Super. 375; 425 A.2d 1151; 1981 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2148


June 29, 1979, Submitted  
February 13, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 554 October Term, 1978, Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence in the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Criminal Division, Nos. 1049-1051, July Term, 1976.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from a judgment of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania) convicting him of simple assault, aggravated assault, criminal conspiracy, and possession of an instrument of crime and sentencing him to a four-year probationary term.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, an off-duty police officer, assaulted and shot a man who had assailed his sister. A police captain who investigated the scene made a passing reference to the City Charter provision when appellant demurred about reporting to the station to give a statement. When appellant arrived at the station and became aware that he might be criminally involved, he volunteered to make a statement in the presence of his lawyer. No statement was taken from appellant until he was fully advised of his Miranda rights. Prior to trial, a judge denied appellant's motion to suppress, finding that the statement was voluntary and was not the product of any coercion resulting from the passing reference to the City Charter provision. The statement was used during the trial and appellant was found guilty of simple assault, aggravated assault, criminal conspiracy, and possession of an instrument of crime and was sentenced to four years probation. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the statement was voluntary and thus was not suppressible, the state established appellant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt, and the impeachment by prior inconsistent statements and rebuttal were proper.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting appellant of simple assault, aggravated assault, criminal conspiracy, and possession of instrument of crime and imposing a four-year probation was affirmed, and the appeal dismissed. Appellant's statement was freely and voluntarily given and was preceded by the Miranda fiat, impeachment by prior inconsistent statements and rebuttal were proper, and the state established appellant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt.

 

591 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Tice v. Nationwide Life Ins. Co.


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


284 Pa. Super. 220; 425 A.2d 782; 1981 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2119


June 13, 1980, Argued  
February 6, 1981, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied July 9, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 2938 October Term, 1978, Appeal from Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County, Trial Division, Civil Section, No. 2580 September Term 1974.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review of the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), that entered judgment by default under local court rules. Appellant failed to answer interrogatories propounded in appellee beneficiary's action in assumpsit to recover the proceeds of an insurance policy. Appellant contended the local rule was invalid because it conflicted with Pa. R. Civ. P. 4019.


OVERVIEW: Appellant insurer sought review of the order of judgment by default entered as a sanction under local court rule, Phila. Ct. R. Civ. P. 145, for appellant's failure to answer interrogatories propounded in appellee beneficiary's action in assumpsit to recover the proceeds of decedent's insurance policy. The court affirmed the order. The court held that local Rule 145 conflicted with Pa. R. Civ. P. 4019 and was invalid. Therefore, the Prothonotary lacked the power to enter a judgment by default against appellee, and the judgment was null and void. The court held that Pa. R. Civ. P. 4019 established a mandatory procedure. Where answers to interrogatories had not been filed, a motion had to be presented to the trial court to determine the default. However, under local Rule 145 no such motion was required. Because of the conflict, the local rule could not stand.


OUTCOME: The order of judgment by default against appellee insurer and in favor of appellee beneficiary was reversed. The local rule was void because it allowed for judgment by default sua sponte, which conflicted with the civil rule that required that a motion be filed before judgment by default could be granted.

 

592 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Linder


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


284 Pa. Super. 327; 425 A.2d 1126; 1981 Pa. Super. LEXIS 2128


September 9, 1980, Argued  
February 6, 1981, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 2064 October Term, 1979, Appeal from Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Criminal Division, No. 4326-78


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County (Pennsylvania), which convicted defendant of theft by deception, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3922.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of theft by deception in violation of 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3922. The court affirmed, finding that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to declare a mistrial due to the prosecution's remarks. The court held that § 3922 was not void for vagueness because the statute gave a person of ordinary intelligence notice that his conduct was forbidden, and because the wording of the statute did not encourage the police and the courts to exercise unfettered discretion. The court further found that defendant's pre-arrest delay of 66 days did not result in any prejudice to defendant and was not sufficient to constitute a denial of due process. The court also determined that the trial court did not err in refusing to give a requested jury instruction as the trial court correctly stated the jury's role in judging a witness' credibility. Finally, the court determined that the trial court properly refused to suppress identifications because the photographic array used was free from impermissible suggestiveness, and, under the totality of the circumstances, the identification of defendant was reliable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of theft by deception because the prosecution's statements did not warrant a mistrial, the theft by deception statute was not void for vagueness, the pre-arrest delay was not prejudicial, the request for jury instruction was properly denied where instructions given correctly stated the law, and the identifications were reliable and properly admitted.

 

593 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. McIlwain School Bus Lines, Inc.


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


283 Pa. Super. 1; 423 A.2d 413; 1980 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3514


November 16, 1979, Submitted  
December 12, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 370 April Term 1979, Appeal from the Order of the Court of Common Pleas of Cambria County, Criminal Division at No. C-358 of 1978.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The commonwealth appealed the order from the Court of Common Pleas of Cambria County (Pennsylvania), which quashed an information that the court held, sua sponte, was insufficient. The information charged defendant school bus corporation with criminal liability for homicide by vehicle in connection with the death of a 6-year-old girl run over after getting off the school bus.


OVERVIEW: A school bus owned by defendant corporation and operated by one of its employees ran over and killed a child who had just gotten off the bus. After defendant was charged with homicide by vehicle, it filed a motion to quash the information against it. The lower court granted defendant's motion to quash, but did not rule on defendant's grounds for the motion, instead holding, sua sponte, that the information issued against defendant was insufficient. The commonwealth appealed. On appeal, the court found that it was error for the trial court to quash the information, sua sponte, as insufficient. The court reversed. The court held that homicide by a vehicle may be committed by "any person who unintentionally caused the death of another person" and that the definition of "person" included a corporation, thus concluding that the defendant could be charged with homicide by vehicle. The court also concluded that the fact that the legislature may have inadvertently failed to provide suitable punishment for the offense when committed by a corporation would not excuse the wrongdoer from prosecution just because it happened to be a corporation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed, holding that it was error for the trial court to quash the information, sua sponte, as insufficient. The court addressed the issue of defendant school bus corporation's liability for homicide, finding statutory provisions and case law to support is conclusion that defendant was liable for the criminal acts of its agents.

 

594 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Norris v. Beck


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


282 Pa. Super. 420; 422 A.2d 1363; 1980 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3414


March 12, 1980, Argued  
November 21, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 401 October Term, 1979, Nos. 352 October Term, 1979 and 1226 October Term, 1979, Appeal from the Orders of the Court of Common Pleas, Criminal Division, for the County of Lehigh at No. 26 April Term, 1962 and No. 3A, 1979


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged an order by the Lehigh County Court of Common Pleas (Pennsylvania), which ordered him to continue to pay child support past the original time period under 18 Pa. Stat. 4323 (1973). Appellant claimed that he should not have been required to continue to pay after the children reached 16 years of age, and that it was improper for trial court to modify the original order.


OVERVIEW: Appellant father was ordered to pay child support for two children that he fathered although out of wedlock. The order was entered and it required payment until the children reached the age of 16 years. However, appellee mother obtained an order extending support obligation under 18 Pa. Crim. Stat. § 4323. The court held that the purpose of the criminal act was to impose the obligation to support children born out of wedlock, converting a moral duty into a legal obligation to provide support until the child's 16th birthday. The court held that no special circumstances existed to warrant the extension, and reversed that order under the criminal code. Appellant claimed the statute of limitation barred any further suit as it required commencement within six years of the birth of the children, or acknowledgement of paternity. The court said that because appellant had pled guilty to bastardy and continually paid support monthly since that time, the statute of limitations had not run, and that he had acknowledged paternity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court modifying the order of support for two more years under the criminal code. However it simultaneously terminated the support order under the civil statute at the child's sixteenth birthday.

 

595 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Oppen v. Callahan


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


282 Pa. Super. 282; 422 A.2d 1117; 1980 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3392


December 5, 1979, Argued  
November 14, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 1130 October Term, 1979 Appeal from an Order in the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Civil Division, No. 78-08271.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contractor challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Montgomery County, Civil Division, which denied his petition under Montgomery County Rule of Civil Procedure No. 807(a)(3) for leave to file an appeal from an award of a Board of Arbitrators in forma pauperis.


OVERVIEW: Appellee homeowners commenced an action against appellant contractor to recover money they allegedly expended in securing another contractor to complete the painting of the exterior of their home in a workmanlike manner. The case was certified to arbitration where, after hearing, the Board of Arbitrators awarded appellees damages, and appellant a lesser amount on his counterclaim. Appellant filed a timely petition to appeal the arbitration award in forma pauperis wherein he alleged that he did not have the necessary funds to pay the security and fees required for appeal. The trial court denied the petition under 5 Pa. Stat. § 72 without a hearing because appellant did not allege that he was impoverished. The court reversed, holding that the absence of a specific allegation "of poverty" was not fatal, and that appellant was entitled to an evidentiary hearing at which time he would have the affirmative burden of proving not only his present inability to pay the appeal costs but also his poverty. The court held that as a condition precedent to the trial court's denial of appellant's petition to proceed in forma pauperis, the trial court was required by section 72 to conduct a hearing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying appellant contractor's petition to proceed with his appeal from an arbitration award in forma pauperis, and remanded with instructions to the lower court to conduct an evidentiary hearing. As a condition precedent to its denial of appellant's petition, the lower court was required by statute to conduct an evidentiary hearing to determine if appellant was impoverished.

 

596 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Smoyer


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


281 Pa. Super. 320; 422 A.2d 189; 1980 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3330


March 19, 1980, Argued  
October 31, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Nos. 1420, 1421 and 1422 October Term, 1979, Appeal from Judgments of Sentence entered June 19, 1979 in the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County at Criminal Nos. 011778 066378 and 066378(a).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from judgments of sentence entered in the Court of Common Pleas of Chester County, Pennsylvania. On appeal, defendant argued that he was denied effective assistance of counsel during trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that counsel was ineffective for failing to move for a directed verdict on the charge of homicide by a vehicle, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3732, for the reason that the statute was unconstitutional. The court disagreed, finding that § 3732 had recently been declared constitutional by the Pennsylvania Supreme Court. However, the court noted that counsel who made the claims of ineffectiveness came from the same public defenders office as trial counsel. At issue was whether a member of the same public defender's office as trial counsel could have raised the issue of ineffective assistance of counsel where it was not obvious that trial counsel was ineffective. The court found that, if a genuine issue of effectiveness of trial counsel existed, then the public defender should have requested the trial court to appoint appellate counsel who was not a member of the public defender's office. The best interest of defendant was not served where his counsel had to establish that an associate from his own office acted in an incompetent manner at trial.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded with directions that the trial court appoint counsel for defendant who was not a member of the Public Defender's Office of Chester County. The appeal would then be given a new briefing schedule and relisted for argument.

Commonwealth v. Waters


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


281 Pa. Super. 535; 422 A.2d 598; 1980 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3245


March 12, 1979, Submitted  
October 24, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 152 March Term, 1978, Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County, Criminal Division, at No. 1662 Crim. Div. 1978.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction by a jury for voluntary deviate sexual intercourse by the Court of Common Pleas of Dauphin County (Pennsylvania). The Pennsylvania Supreme Court held that the statute under which appellant was convicted, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 3101 (1973), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted by a jury of soliciting an undercover state trooper to commit voluntary deviate sexual intercourse. Appellant claimed that the sections of the crimes code dealing with voluntary deviate sexual intercourse, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. §§ 3101, 3124, were unconstitutional. The court found that the Pennsylvania Supreme Court had held that the statute prohibiting voluntary deviate sexual intercourse between unmarried partners was unconstitutional as a denial of equal protection of the laws. Because the statute under which appellant was convicted was constitutionally defective, the court ruled that it must reverse the judgment of sentence and discharge appellant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction for voluntary deviate sexual intercourse because the Pennsylvania Supreme Court determined that the statute under which appellant was convicted was constitutionally defective.

 

598 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Jackson


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


281 Pa. Super. 310; 422 A.2d 184; 1980 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3268


December 6, 1979, Submitted  
October 24, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied March 13, 1981.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 153 October Term, 1979, Appeal from the Judgment of Sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Huntingdon County, Criminal Division, at No. 77-184


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the entry of sentence of the Court of Common Pleas of Huntingdon County (Pennsylvania), which found defendant guilty of possession of weapons or implements of escape.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought review of his conviction of possessing weapons or implements of escape. Defendant alleged on appeal that he was improperly convicted of the offense and that 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 5122(a)(3), was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the entry of sentence, holding that the evidence, when viewed in the light most favorable to the commonwealth, supported the finding by the lower court that defendant, while an inmate, did unlawfully have in his possession or under his control an implement of escape, namely, a hacksaw blade. The court also concluded that § 5122(a)(3) was not unconstitutional despite defendant's assertion that the language of the statute did not state precisely what was meant by "under his control." The court held that the fact that the legislature could have chosen clear and more precise language equally capable of achieving the end which it sought did not mean that the statute was unconstitutionally vague. The court further held that § 5122(a)(3) gave adequate notice to a person of ordinary intelligence that the conduct which formed the basis of the charge was forbidden by statute and, thus, was constitutional under the due process standard.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the entry of sentence, holding that the evidence supported the lower court's finding that defendant, while an inmate, unlawfully had in his possession an implement of escape. The court further held that the statute under which defendant was convicted gave adequate notice that the conduct which formed the basis of the charge was forbidden and, thus, was constitutional under the due process standard.

600 of 1476 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Faust


Superior Court of Pennsylvania


281 Pa. Super. 357; 422 A.2d 208; 1980 Pa. Super. LEXIS 3235


April 16, 1980, Argued  
October 10, 1980, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 101 April Term, 1979, Appeal from Order of Court of Common Pleas of Washington County, Criminal Division, at Nos. 708 and 793 of 1978, Entered on January 5, 1979.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The commonwealth appealed the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Washington County (Pennsylvania), which suppressed evidence discovered in a warrantless search of a public bathroom stall, in defendants' prosecutions for voluntary deviate sexual intercourse.


OVERVIEW: The commonwealth appealed from an order suppressing evidence discovered in a warrantless search of a public bathroom stall. As a result of the search, defendants were charged with violations of Voluntary Deviate Sexual Intercourse statute, 18 Pa. Cons. Stat. Ann. § 3124. The court found that subsequent to the filing of the appeal, that statute was found to be unconstitutional. Additionally, the court found that the suppression issue raised by the commonwealth was moot, and an appeal could not lie. Accordingly, the commonwealth's appeal was dismissed.


OUTCOME: The commonwealth's appeal of the trial court's suppression of evidence was dismissed because the suppression issue was moot as the statute upon which defendants were charged had been deemed unconstitutional.
